I found a little out-of-the-way bakery today that had homemade pastries and pies. I bought two pies (banana cream ND strawberry rhubarb) for my coworkers bday and they were absolutely delicious! Everyone took their first bite and there was a magical pause... And sigh of happiness. The woman who helped me, whom I assume is Mel, gave me a discount on one of the pies because the crust broke as she was putting it in a box! I'm definitely coming back here to try more of their scrumptious pastries and cakes!</review>

I like the new exposure to the array of Mexican dishes outside of what we see in typical Mexican food establishments at a reasonable price.

The admosphere is casual. The restaurant is in a run-down area of town.</review>< Gmap_id>

< review>
Does the thought of Sopes, Huaraches, Enomoladas, Enfrioladas, Chile Rellen√≥s or Sopa de Fideo (just name a few) make your mouth water? Then this is the place for you!  The food here is authentic AF. The plates are so delicious and very homemade. Their salsas are awesome especially the Chile de √Årbol. We had the Chicken Flautas and they were a meal in itself - done just like in CDMX. We also had the Enchiladas Verdes and the green sauce was incredible. The enchiladas were generously filled with chicken too. We also had a bowl of their Sopa de Fideo which was also very good. Actually it was awesome! I'm going to try and make my sopa de fideo like they do here - they kindly gave me their recipe.

So, if you're Jonesing for Tex-Mex or Cal-Mex food, this isn't the place. But, if you want truly incredible, authentic Mexican food, this is place for just that.

This place is new and family owned. The service was outstanding. Please do not hesitate - this is the real deal for authentic Mexican Chilango dishes. Your taste buds are in for a treat - you will not regret it.<//review>

<name>Daniel Farias<//name>< Date>
1561153526534< /Date>
<rate>4< /rate><Review>A really solid find in San Bernardino. The surrounding area isn't pretty but Nopal is pretty clean inside. The entire dining room could use a facelift but is otherwise in solid condition. Customer service is good, the lady who helped us out was very friendly. Prices are also comparable to most other Mexican establishments so that's good.

I've eaten a lot (and I mean a lot) of Mexican food but I've never seen a "Pamborazo" on the menu. 9 out of 10 times I'd go with tacos or enchiladas but considering I'd never had this before I decided to try it. This Pamborazo is basically a torta dipped in guajillo sauce and it comes with beans, chorizo, potatoes, lettuce, queso fresco and sour cream. Typically I would find something to pick on but in this case I wouldn't change a thing on this sandwich. My wife's huarache de asada was pretty good but the taco and complimentary chips and salsa were ok.

All in all this was a very good food stop. Customer service was good, food was good and an old dining room. If I'm ever in the area again I would definitely come back for more.< /Review>< Pictures>

They directed me to the Apple Store, so I went. The Apple Store wanted to swap my SIM, and restore the phone as new. I came for oil change and smog inspection. I was required to leave and drive the car for smog because I recently had to replace the battery which caused the monitors to not be ready for the test. After driving the car and preparing the monitors, I returned for the test. It passed. I was rather disappointed to return to pick up the car and find that it was left with the key on in the accessory position and the radio and air turned on. My battery gauge shows low and it started but only barely. It shows a real lack of professionalism for a mechanic to fail to consider the charge level in a battery enough to simply remove the keys after completing their work. Additionally, I brought it in with a tire light on, figuring that since I was going two blocks to them for service, I'd let them check and set the tire pressure and the light would go off without having to get my hands dirty. After I picked up the car, I noticed the light was still on. I checked the paperwork and the inspection showed they set all 4 tires to spec. I considered a sensor might be going bad. It turns out that the light was on because 1 tire was at 25lbs. After filling it myself the light went off. Basically it seems they charge the fees and give you paperwork but as far as working on the car they do as little as possible... I'm a mechanic so it's easy for me to spot an honest, hard-working professional and it's easy to see when they're not. I got the paperwork for smog and I assume fresh oil, which is what I paid and asked for but I expected something just a little more. I'll go somewhere else next time.<//Text></record>

< Text>
SCAM. ARTISTS. TL;DR, these guys tried to extract about $900 dollars in unnecessary services from me. Please read further for details:

I do not ever write business reviews because I never feel strongly enough to do so, but my experience today has changed that. I brought my car in for a rough idle yesterday and was told that I needed to leave it overnight and pay for a $99 diagnostic workup. This amounted to extracting the OBD code (which can be done for free at O'Reilly just down the street). I was called this morning and told that I needed to replace all of my spark plugs and ignition coils at the price of ~$1,100, with the breakdown being ~$80 for labor, with the rest being attributed to parts, and that they would do a free fuel injector and throttle body cleaning. I asked why the parts were so expensive and I was told that it was "because this car requires iridium spark plugs and they are very expensive", and that my car model (Toyota Corolla)for some reason required 2 plugs (or 2 coils? this part was unclear...) for each cylinder. I grew up doing some maintenance on my own car and my family's cars, and all of this was a bit suspicious to me (I knew it was 1 spark plug and 1 ignition coil per each of my 4 cylinders), so I started looking into how much these parts cost:

Cost for 4 OEM spark plugs at O'Reilly: $27
Cost for 4 OEM ignition coils at O'Reilly: $360
Add in the proposed $80 cost of labor for a grand total of: $467... $633 less than what they proposed the job would cost.

I pressed Mike on why the parts were so expensive, quoting the cost at the neighboring auto parts store, and he told me that they have to buy at an incredibly high markup. At this point I decided to just pick up my car and do it myself since I have tools, it's an easy job, and O'Reilly was on the way.

When I picked the vehicle up, Mike went on to explain how the cost of the "free" fuel injector and throttle body cleaning is actually wrapped up in the cost of the parts, and that's why the parts were so expensive. This is obviously a deceptive practice at face. I then asked if there was any way to tell which ignition coil was acting up, and he explained "No, this is a general code and there's no way to tell. All ignition coils should be replaced." I looked up the code,  P0302: Cylinder 2 Misfire - i.e. it is a problem with either the ignition coil or spark plug of the second cylinder (again... of 4 cylinders). There are codes P0301-P0308 for engines with up to 8 cylinders, and obviously the last number indicates the affected cylinder. So the whole pitch about having to replace all ignition cylinders was a lie.

I went to O'Reilly down the street and bought my $27 set of 4x iridium spark plugs, and a single $90 ignition coil (both OEM) costing me a total of $117 (and after 30 mins of wrenching, completely solved the issue). While I was there I saw a Midas employee buying parts for a repair, so one could assume they paid a similar expense for parts. Again, assuming they would have bought all of the same parts I did, at the same cost, and I allowed them to replace all 4 ignition coils unnecessarily, the job should have cost $467. Subtract that from the proposed cost of the job, and they were overcharging me by $723 IF I just unwittingly said ok to replacing all 4 ignition coils. If they did the job that was actually needed (1 coil, and 4 spark plugs - and its hard to say if all spark plugs were necessary but they're cheap and I don't know the last time they were replaced), I would have been overcharged by $903. For what? The fuel injector cleaning I was told I needed? Seafoam costs $8. Throttle body cleaning? Only labor there...

So... attempted $900 overcharge (ignoring the $99 "diagnostic"). I understand money is tight for all businesses right now, but this was just absurdly unethical. I will never be taking my car here again.< /Text>

<user>116057423051652783274</user><review>I needed an oil change done for my car because it was due for a while. After looking at many places around PB being shady as hell or closed based on reviews, I decided on here.

Pros: Cool guys working there, did the oil change decently fast and for 25 dollars for my Scion XB. Very knowledgable staff and were open and honest in showing me everything that they were doing. For a strictly oil change trip, very good for the price.

Cons: Not much to say since its mostly my fault for asking the guy working on my car to keep an eye out for anything else just in case, but they informed me my filters needed changing asap and that my windshield wipers needed to be changed immediately or they'll scratch my windshield. (This was on a rainy day.)

They'll try to upsell you a little bit but it's expected sort of in a way. I can't really fault them for trying being a salesman myself.

4 stars from me for being knowledgable and very helpful and swift working, just be cautious of the fact that you'll probably get talked into paying more, although in my case it being highly recommended anyway to do it quick simply because I have a long commute anyway. <userid>104162771020685923386<//userid><username>Patrick Tuminaro<//username><time>1514875200125<//time><Rating>5<//Rating>< Review>
The best option for all you can eat sushi in the Antelope Valley. Chefs and servers are swift and courteous. The food is presented well and they allow "easy rice"and half-roll ordering which let's you sample a broad array of their offerings. Price is on the higher end of the spectrum for lunch in the area but is worth spending for the unhurried AYCE dining. A top of advice, the waits to get seated at the bar on a popular night can top 45 min so if you are headed out on "date night" do yourself a favor and call to have your name put on the list in advance. < review>
Best sushi I ever had, bar none. For the Antelope Valley, it's crazy that we find a restaurant this good when about everything else is garbage. Even on an international point if view, it's litterally amazing!

The fish is fresh, delicious, tender, buttery and their interpretations of the classics are phenomenal. You NEED to try the "Maine Roll" (a baked lobster sushi concoction that's just demented).

They have a "all you can eat" sushi bar and happy hour sak√©, so bring your appetite and enjoy sushi after sushi until your belly pops.

I much prefer the ambiance of this small restaurant (compared to the Palmdale location) as it feels more Japan-typical and cozy.

Definitely a 10/10 for me!< /review>

< Review>
A friends couple invited us to lunch. They go there every Saturday religiously. We were seated, drink orders taken, and we waited patiently for our appetizers. Our wives got their salad and soup in a timely manner, apps arrived in a decent amount of time. Then all he'll broke loose. My wife received her entree, then 5 mins later our companion's wife got her entree. Then 5 mins passed. Then 10. Then I had to ask for a refill after my waitress walked by 3 times. Still no entree for me or my friend. Finally asked the waitress where our food was.  She apologized, and went to check. 4 mins later a different person brought my roll out, dropped it in front of me, and walked off. I said "About time", to which he replied back, mimicking me in a sarcastic tone"About time". I stood up and went to the manager, filed a complaint and left.

4 tables were served their entire meal while I waited. I was offered little apology.

First and last time I go there.</Review>
